<p><b>Sofia</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/Àà/ primary stress follows">Àà</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/o ä/ long 'o' in 'code'">o ä</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/…ô/ 'a' in 'about'">…ô</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/Àà/ primary stress follows">Àà</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/…í/ short 'o' in 'body'">…í</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/…ô/ 'a' in 'about'">…ô</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/o ä/ long 'o' in 'code'">o ä</span><span title="/Àà/ primary stress follows">Àà</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/iÀê/ long 'e' in 'seed'">iÀê</span><span title="/…ô/ 'a' in 'about'">…ô</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>) (<a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>: <span lang="bg" xml:lang="bg">–°–æ—Ñ–∏—è</span>, <i>Sofiya</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Bulgarian_and_Macedonian" title="Help:IPA for Bulgarian and Macedonian">[Ààs…îfi…ô, Ààs…îfj…ô]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<a href="/wiki/File:Sofia.ogg" title="File:Sofia.ogg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a> <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/32/Sofia.ogg" class="internal" title="Sofia.ogg">listen</a>)</small>) is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Bulgaria" title="List of cities and towns in Bulgaria">largest city</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>. The city has a population of 1.26 million, while over 1.5 million people live in its functional urban area. It is the largest <a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">South Slavic</a> city in the world, being slightly more populous than Belgrade. The city is located at the foot of <a href="/wiki/Vitosha" title="Vitosha">Vitosha</a> Mountain in the western part of the country, within less than 50 kilometres (31&#160;mi) drive from the <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbian</a> border. Its location in the centre of the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan peninsula">Balkan peninsula</a> means that it is the midway between the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a>, whereas the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a> is the closest to it.<sup id="cite_ref-tr_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tr-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sofia has been an area of <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_time_of_continuous_habitation" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities by time of continuous habitation">human habitation</a> since at least 7000 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-ghodsee_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghodsee-3">[3]</a></sup> Being Bulgaria's <a href="/wiki/Primate_city" title="Primate city">primate city</a>, Sofia is a hometown of many of the major local <a href="/wiki/Universities" class="mw-redirect" title="Universities">universities</a>, cultural <a href="/wiki/Institution" title="Institution">institutions</a> and commercial companies.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Sofia is one of the top 10 best places for start-up business in the world, especially in IT technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Sofia is Europe's most affordable capital to visit as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names">Names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sredets_seal_1878.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Sredets_seal_1878.jpg/200px-Sredets_seal_1878.jpg" width="200" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Sredets_seal_1878.jpg/300px-Sredets_seal_1878.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Sredets_seal_1878.jpg/400px-Sredets_seal_1878.jpg 2x" data-file-width="404" data-file-height="219" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sredets_seal_1878.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The first seal of the city from 1878 which calls it <i>Sredets</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For the longest time the city possessed<sup id="cite_ref-constantine_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constantine-19">[19]</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Thracian_language" title="Thracian language">Thracian</a> name, derived from the tribe <i><a href="/wiki/Serdi" title="Serdi">Serdi</a></i>, who were either of <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracian</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tr_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tr-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-The_Cambridge_Ancient_History_1992.2C_page_600_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Cambridge_Ancient_History_1992.2C_page_600-20">[20]</a></sup> or mixed Thracian-Celtic origin.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The Serdi and the name of emperor <a href="/wiki/Traian" class="mw-redirect" title="Traian">Marcus Ulpius Traianus</a> (53 ‚Äì 117 AD) prompted the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a> to give the city the combinative name of <i><a href="/wiki/Ulpia_(gens)" title="Ulpia (gens)">Ulpia</a> Serdica</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-world_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-books.google.bg_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.bg-24">[24]</a></sup> Ulpia is derived from an Umbrian cognate of the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> word <i>lupus</i>, meaning "wolf."<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> It seems that the first written mention of <i>Serdica</i> was made during his reign and the last mention was in the 19th century in a Bulgarian text (–°–∞—Ä–¥–∞–∫—ñ–∏, <i>Sardaki</i>). During the Romans <i>civitas Serdenisium</i> was mentioned the "brightest city of the Serdi" in official inscriptions. The city was major throughout the past ever since Antiquity,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="I don't see this in the Emperor Constantine citation that follows (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> when Roman emperor <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">Constantine the Great</a> referred to it as "my Rome", and it nearly became his capital.<sup id="cite_ref-constantine_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constantine-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other names given to Sofia, such as <i>Serdonpolis</i> (Œ£ŒµœÅŒ¥œéŒΩ œÄœåŒªŒπœÇ, "City of the Serdi") and <i>Triaditza</i> (Œ§œÅŒπŒ¨Œ¥ŒπœÑŒ∂Œ±, "Trinity"), were mentioned by <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> sources or coins. The Slavic name <i>Sredets</i> (–°—Ä—£–¥–µ—Ü—ä), which is related to "middle" (—Å—Ä–µ–¥–∞, "sreda") and to the city's earliest name, first appeared on paper in an 11th-century text. The city was called <i>Atralissa</i> by the Arab traveler <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_al-Idrisi" title="Muhammad al-Idrisi">Idrisi</a> and <i>Strelisa</i>, <i>Stralitsa</i> or <i>Stralitsion</i> by the <a href="/wiki/Crusaders" class="mw-redirect" title="Crusaders">Crusaders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The name <i>Sofia</i> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Sofia_Church,_Sofia" title="Saint Sofia Church, Sofia">Saint Sofia Church</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> as opposed to the prevailing <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bulgaria_province_name_etymologies" title="List of Bulgaria province name etymologies">etymology among Bulgarian cities and towns</a>. It is ultimately derived from the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_language" title="Egyptian language">Egyptian</a> <a href="/wiki/Kemetism" title="Kemetism">Kemetic</a> word <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/sb3" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:sb3">sb√Ö</a></i> (ìã¥ìÉÄìÑøìáºìá≥), meaning "star, door, teaching and wisdom" and attested first in the 20th century BC in the tomb of <a href="/wiki/Intef_I" title="Intef I">Intef I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bernal1987_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bernal1987-31">[31]</a></sup> This was a tradition of collection of wise literature, shared between <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> cultures, which was called <i><a href="/wiki/Sophia_(wisdom)" title="Sophia (wisdom)">sophia</a></i> (œÉŒøœÜŒØŒ±) in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Greek language">Greek</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The earliest works where this latest name is registered are the duplicate of the Gospel of Serdica, in a dialog between two salesmen from <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">Dubrovnik</a> around 1359, in the 14th-century Vitosha Charter of Bulgarian tsar <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Shishman_of_Bulgaria" title="Ivan Shishman of Bulgaria">Ivan Shishman</a> and in a <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ragusa" title="Republic of Ragusa">Ragusan</a> merchant's notes of 1376.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In these documents the city is called <i>Sofia</i>, but at the same time the region and the city's inhabitants are still called <i>Sredecheski</i> (—Å—Ä—£–¥–µ—á—å—Å–∫–æ–∏, "of Sredets"), which continued until the 20th century. The city became somehow popular to the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottomans</a> by the name <i>Sofya</i> (ÿµŸàŸÅŸäŸá). In 1879 there was a dispute about what the name of the new Bulgarian capital should be, when the citizens created a committee of famous people, insisting for the Slavic name. Gradually, a compromise arose, officialisation of <i>Sofia</i> for the nationwide institutions, while legitimating the title <i>Sredets</i> for the administrative and church institutions, before the latter was abandoned through the years.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city's name is pronounced by Bulgarians with a stress on the 'o', in contrast with the tendency of foreigners to place the stress on 'i'. The female given name "Sofia" is pronounced by Bulgarians with a stress on the 'i'.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:808px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vitosa.jpg" class="image" title="The skyline of Sofia, Bulgaria, with the Vitosha mountain in the background during winter"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Vitosa.jpg/800px-Vitosa.jpg" width="800" height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Vitosa.jpg/1200px-Vitosa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Vitosa.jpg/1600px-Vitosa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="585" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vitosa.jpg" title="File:Vitosa.jpg"></a></div>
The skyline of Sofia, Bulgaria, with the <a href="/wiki/Vitosha" title="Vitosha">Vitosha</a> mountain in the background during winter</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sofia has an area of 492&#160;km<sup>2</sup>, while <a href="/wiki/Sofia_City_Province" title="Sofia City Province">Sofia City Province</a> has an area of 1344&#160;km<sup>2</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Sofia's development as a significant settlement owes much to its central position in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>. It is situated in western Bulgaria, at the northern foot of the <a href="/wiki/Vitosha" title="Vitosha">Vitosha</a> mountain, in the <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Valley" title="Sofia Valley">Sofia Valley</a> that is surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan mountains">Balkan mountains</a> to the north. The valley has an average altitude of 550 metres (1,800&#160;ft). Unlike most European capitals, Sofia does not have any large rivers or bridges, but is surrounded by comparatively high mountains on all sides. Three <a href="/wiki/Mountain_pass" title="Mountain pass">mountain passes</a> lead to the city, which have been key roads since antiquity, Vitosha being the watershed between <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Seas</a>. A number of low rivers cross the city, including the <a href="/wiki/Vladaya_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Vladaya River">Vladayska</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Perlovska" title="Perlovska">Perlovska</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Iskar_(river)" title="Iskar (river)">Iskar River</a> in its upper course flows <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">near eastern</a> Sofia. The city is known for its 49 <a href="/wiki/Spring_(hydrosphere)" class="mw-redirect" title="Spring (hydrosphere)">mineral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hot_spring" title="Hot spring">thermal</a> springs. Artificial and dam lakes were built in the twentieth century. The 1818 Sofia earthquake was a 6.0‚Äì7.2 <a href="/wiki/Medvedev%E2%80%93Sponheuer%E2%80%93Karnik_scale" title="Medvedev‚ÄìSponheuer‚ÄìKarnik scale">Medvedev‚ÄìSponheuer‚ÄìKarnik</a> Scale earthquake, the 1858 earthquake was an 6,6 same scale earthquake though reaching up to 10 in parts such as <a href="/wiki/Boyana" title="Boyana">Boyana</a>, this was followed by a 7‚Äì8 MSK Sofia earthquake in 1917 and finally by the <a href="/wiki/2012_Pernik_earthquake" title="2012 Pernik earthquake">2012 Pernik earthquake</a> which was a 5.6 <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">M<sub>w</sub></a> (or 5.8 <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" title="Richter magnitude scale">M<sub>L</sub></a>)<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">magnitude</a> <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">earthquake</a>. The <a href="/wiki/2014_Aegean_Sea_earthquake" title="2014 Aegean Sea earthquake">2014 Aegean Sea earthquake</a> was also noticed in the city.</p>
<p>Air pollution is a problem in Sofia due to its location in the Sofia valley, which is surrounded by mountains that reduce the ability of the air to self-clean. The air is polluted mostly by <a href="/wiki/Particulate_matter" class="mw-redirect" title="Particulate matter">particulate matters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">nitrogen oxides</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Sofia has the most polluted air of any capital in the <a href="/wiki/EU" class="mw-redirect" title="EU">EU</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sofia has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K√∂ppen climate classification">K√∂ppen climate classification</a> <i>Dfb</i>) with an average annual temperature of 10.6&#160;¬∞C (51.1&#160;¬∞F).</p>
<p>Winters are cold and snowy. In the coldest days temperatures can drop below ‚àí15&#160;¬∞C (5&#160;¬∞F), most notably in January. The lowest recorded temperature is ‚àí28.3&#160;¬∞C (‚àí19&#160;¬∞F) (January 24, 1942).<sup id="cite_ref-stringmeteo.com_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stringmeteo.com-39">[39]</a></sup> Fog is not unusual, especially in the beginning of the season. On average, Sofia receives a total snowfall of 97&#160;cm (38.2&#160;in) and 58 days with snow cover.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The snowiest recorded winter was 1995/1996 with a total snowfall of 171&#160;cm (67.3&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The record snow depth is 57&#160;cm (22.4&#160;in) (December 25, 2001).<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Summers are warm and sunny. In summer, the city generally remains slightly cooler than other parts of Bulgaria, due to its higher altitude. However, the city is also subjected to heat waves with high temperatures reaching or exceeding 35&#160;¬∞C (95&#160;¬∞F) in the hottest days, particularly in July and August. The highest recorded temperature is 41&#160;¬∞C (106&#160;¬∞F) (July 5, 2000 and July 24, 2007).<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The hottest recorded summer was in 2012 with a daily average July temperature of 24.8&#160;¬∞C (76.6&#160;¬∞F).<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>Springs and autumns in Sofia are relatively short with variable and dynamic weather, intensive storms, sudden cold or heat waves.</p>
<p>The city receives an average precipitation of 581.8&#160;mm (22.91&#160;in) a year, reaching its peak in late spring and early summer when <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorms" class="mw-redirect" title="Thunderstorms">thunderstorms</a> are common. The wettest recorded year was 2014 with a total precipitation of 1,066.6&#160;mm (41.99&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_and_antiquity">Prehistory and antiquity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Prehistory and antiquity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bronze_coin_of_Serdi_Celts.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Bronze_coin_of_Serdi_Celts.jpg/300px-Bronze_coin_of_Serdi_Celts.jpg" width="300" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Bronze_coin_of_Serdi_Celts.jpg/450px-Bronze_coin_of_Serdi_Celts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Bronze_coin_of_Serdi_Celts.jpg/600px-Bronze_coin_of_Serdi_Celts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2048" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Remains_of_Serdica_fortress_walls_in_the_basement_of_central_market_hall_Sofia_20090406_002.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Remains_of_Serdica_fortress_walls_in_the_basement_of_central_market_hall_Sofia_20090406_002.JPG/200px-Remains_of_Serdica_fortress_walls_in_the_basement_of_central_market_hall_Sofia_20090406_002.JPG" width="200" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Remains_of_Serdica_fortress_walls_in_the_basement_of_central_market_hall_Sofia_20090406_002.JPG/300px-Remains_of_Serdica_fortress_walls_in_the_basement_of_central_market_hall_Sofia_20090406_002.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Remains_of_Serdica_fortress_walls_in_the_basement_of_central_market_hall_Sofia_20090406_002.JPG/400px-Remains_of_Serdica_fortress_walls_in_the_basement_of_central_market_hall_Sofia_20090406_002.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4272" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Remains_of_Serdica_fortress_walls_in_the_basement_of_central_market_hall_Sofia_20090406_002.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A restored city plan of Roman Serdica under <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Aurelius" title="Marcus Aurelius">Marcus Aurelius</a> (161‚Äì180)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sofia has been an area of continuous human habitation since at least the 8th millennium BC,<sup id="cite_ref-ghodsee_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghodsee-3">[3]</a></sup> but others have inhabited the area 30,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-Routledge_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Routledge-55">[55]</a></sup> The city has a history of nearly 7000 years and it is the second oldest city in Europe according to the city's official website and other sources, though the meaning of the claim is unclear as in the world there were hardly any cities at the time. In the context, certainly the neolithic village in <a href="/wiki/Slatina,_Sofia" title="Slatina, Sofia">Slatina</a>, dating to the 5th‚Äì6th millennium BC, is described.<sup id="cite_ref-sofia.bg_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sofia.bg-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sofia.bg_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sofia.bg-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2nd_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2nd-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7000bc_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7000bc-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-plants_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plants-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> However, the motto of the city is "grows, but does not age". Remains from another neolithic settlement around the <a href="/wiki/National_Art_Gallery_(Bulgaria)" title="National Art Gallery (Bulgaria)">National Art Gallery</a> are traced to the 3rd‚Äì4th millennium BC, which has been the traditional center of the city ever since and is not changed today.<sup id="cite_ref-sofiaculture.bg_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sofiaculture.bg-61">[61]</a></sup> The earliest tribes who settled were the <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracians</a>. In 1400 ‚Äì 1300 BC. Sofia's area was populated by the Thracian tribe of <a href="/wiki/Tilataei" title="Tilataei">Tilataei</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> invasion in 3rd century BC Tilataei were conquered by the Celtic tribe of <a href="/wiki/Serdi" title="Serdi">Serdi</a>. The Celts were assimilated by the local Thracian population during the late <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period" title="Hellenistic period">Hellenistic period</a> in 2nd ‚Äì 1st century BC.<sup id="cite_ref-Marazov.2C_Ivan_1998_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marazov.2C_Ivan_1998-5">[5]</a></sup> According to some sources, it got first an official mention in the 7th/8th century BC when the <a href="/wiki/Serdi" title="Serdi">Serdi</a> (Sardi) as a <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracian</a> tribe established a settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7000bc_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7000bc-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Other sources suppose that the Serdi's <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> origin is convincingly evidenced through linguistic and archeological clues but that their presence is not evidenced before the 1st century BC,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> whereas others assume their mixed Thracian-Celtic origin or relation to the <a href="/wiki/Sardinians" class="mw-redirect" title="Sardinians">Sards</a>. The earliest evidence of Celtic presence in the Sofia area (<a href="/wiki/Pernik" title="Pernik">Pernik</a>) can be from the 3rd century BC.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Some clues lead to the conclusion that the area of the settlement was between <a href="/wiki/TZUM" title="TZUM">TZUM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheraton_Hotel" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheraton Hotel">Sheraton Hotel</a> and the Presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-sofiaculture.bg_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sofiaculture.bg-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> In the 500s BC, the area became part of a <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracian</a> state union, called the <a href="/wiki/Odrysian_kingdom" title="Odrysian kingdom">Odrysian kingdom</a>, when another Thracian tribe appeared in the town, the <a href="/wiki/Odrysses" class="mw-redirect" title="Odrysses">Odrysses</a>. For a short period the Thracian rule was possibly interrupted by the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>. In 339 BC <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Macedon" title="Philip II of Macedon">Philip II of Macedon</a> destroyed and ravaged the town which was its first time.<sup id="cite_ref-Routledge_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Routledge-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Around BC 29, Serdica was conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, gradually becoming the most important Roman city of the region.<sup id="cite_ref-world_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-books.google.bg_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.bg-24">[24]</a></sup> It became a <i>municipium</i> during the reign of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Trajan" title="Trajan">Trajan</a> (98‚Äì117). Serdica expanded, as <a href="/wiki/Turret" title="Turret">turrets</a>, protective walls, <a href="/wiki/Public_bathing" title="Public bathing">public baths</a>, administrative and cult buildings, a civic <a href="/wiki/Basilica" title="Basilica">basilica</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Amphitheatre" title="Amphitheatre">amphitheatre</a>, a circus, the <a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">City Council</a> (Boul√©), a large forum, a big circus (theatre), etc. were built. Serdica was a significant midway city on the Roman road <a href="/wiki/Via_Militaris" title="Via Militaris">Via Militaris</a>, connecting <a href="/wiki/Singidunum" title="Singidunum">Singidunum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Byzantium" title="Byzantium">Byzantium</a>. In the 3rd century, it became the capital of <a href="/wiki/Dacia_Aureliana" title="Dacia Aureliana">Dacia Aureliana</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> and when Emperor <a href="/wiki/Diocletian" title="Diocletian">Diocletian</a> divided the province of Dacia Aureliana into Dacia Ripensis (at the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Dacia_(Roman_province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dacia (Roman province)">Dacia Mediterranea</a>, Serdica became the capital of the latter. Serdica's citizens of <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracian</a> descent were referred to as <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrians</a><sup id="cite_ref-Routledge_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Routledge-55">[55]</a></sup> probably because it was at some time the capital of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Illyria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eastern Illyria (page does not exist)">Eastern Illyria</a> (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Illyria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Second Illyria (page does not exist)">Second Illyria</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> For future emperors Serdica was their residence form where they ruled Rome.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Festung_Serdica_Sofia_20090405_006.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Festung_Serdica_Sofia_20090405_006.JPG/230px-Festung_Serdica_Sofia_20090405_006.JPG" width="230" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Festung_Serdica_Sofia_20090405_006.JPG/345px-Festung_Serdica_Sofia_20090405_006.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Festung_Serdica_Sofia_20090405_006.JPG/460px-Festung_Serdica_Sofia_20090405_006.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Festung_Serdica_Sofia_20090405_006.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The fortification of Serdica</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Roman emperors <a href="/wiki/Aurelian" title="Aurelian">Aurelian</a> (215‚Äì275)<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Galerius" title="Galerius">Galerius</a> (260‚Äì311)<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> were from Serdica. The city subsequently expanded for a century and a half, it became a significant political and economical centre, more so&#160;‚Äî it became one of the first Roman cities where Christianity was recognized as an <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">official religion</a> (under <a href="/wiki/Galerius" title="Galerius">Galerius</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Edict_of_Toleration_by_Galerius" title="Edict of Toleration by Galerius">Edict of Toleration by Galerius</a> was issued in 311 in Serdica by the Roman emperor Galerius, officially ending the Diocletianic persecution of Christianity. The Edict implicitly granted Christianity the status of "<a href="/wiki/Religio_licita" title="Religio licita">religio licita</a>", a worship recognized and accepted by the Roman Empire. It was the first edict legalizing Christianity, preceding the <a href="/wiki/Edict_of_Milan" title="Edict of Milan">Edict of Milan</a> by two years. For <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">Constantine the Great</a> it was 'Sardica mea Roma est' (Serdica is my Rome). He considered making Serdica the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> instead of Constantinople.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> which was already not dissimilar to a <a href="/wiki/Tetrarchy" title="Tetrarchy">tetrarchic</a> capital of the Roman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In 343 AD, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Sardica" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Sardica">Council of Sardica</a> was held in the city, in a church located where the current 6th century <a href="/wiki/Hagia_Sophia_Church_(Sofia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hagia Sophia Church (Sofia)">Church of Saint Sophia</a> was later built.</p>
<p>The city was destroyed in the <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_II#Wars_with_the_Huns.2C_Vandals.2C_and_Persians" title="Theodosius II">447 invasion</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a> and the city laid in ruins for a century<sup id="cite_ref-Routledge_55-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Routledge-55">[55]</a></sup> It was rebuilt by <a href="/wiki/List_of_Byzantine_emperors" title="List of Byzantine emperors">Byzantine Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">Justinian I</a>. During the reign of Justinian it flourished, being surrounded with great fortress walls whose remnants can still be seen today.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages.2C_Renaissance_and_early_modern_history">Middle Ages, Renaissance and early modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Middle Ages, Renaissance and early modern history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city first became part of the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a> during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Krum" title="Krum">Khan Krum</a> in 809, after a long <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Serdica_(809)" title="Siege of Serdica (809)">siege</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Afterw–∞rds, it grew into an important fortress and administrative centre when <a href="/wiki/Omurtag_of_Bulgaria" title="Omurtag of Bulgaria">Khan Omurtag</a> made it a center of Sredets province (Sredetski komitat, –°—Ä–µ–¥–µ—Ü–∫–∏ –∫–æ–º–∏—Ç–∞—Ç). After the conquest of the Bulgarian capital <a href="/wiki/Preslav" class="mw-redirect" title="Preslav">Preslav</a> by <a href="/wiki/Sviatoslav_I_of_Kiev" title="Sviatoslav I of Kiev">Sviatoslav I of Kiev</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_I_Tzimiskes" title="John I Tzimiskes">John I Tzimiskes</a>' armies in 970‚Äì971, the Bulgarian Patriarch Damyan chose Sofia for his seat in the next year and the capital of Bulgaria was first moved to Sredets.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> In the second half of 10th century the city was ruled by <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_(komes)" title="Nicholas (komes)">Komit Nikola</a> and his sons, popular as "<a href="/wiki/Cometopuli_dynasty" title="Cometopuli dynasty">Komitopuli</a>". One of them is <a href="/wiki/Samuel_of_Bulgaria" title="Samuel of Bulgaria">Samuil</a>, who became an Emperor of Bulgaria in 997. After a number of unsuccessful sieges, the city fell to the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> in 1018, but once again was incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Second_Bulgarian_Empire" title="Second Bulgarian Empire">restored Bulgarian Empire</a> at the time of Tsar <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Asen_I_of_Bulgaria" title="Ivan Asen I of Bulgaria">Ivan Asen I</a>.</p>
<p>In 1382, Sofia was seized by the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> in the course of the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian%E2%80%93Ottoman_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian‚ÄìOttoman Wars">Bulgarian-Ottoman Wars</a> after a long siege. Around 1393 it became the seat of newly established <a href="/wiki/Sanjak_of_Sofia" title="Sanjak of Sofia">Sanjak of Sofia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city was occupied by Hungarian forces for a short time in 1443. After the failed crusade of <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_III_of_Poland" title="W≈Çadys≈Çaw III of Poland">W≈Çadys≈Çaw III of Poland</a> in 1443 towards Sofia, the city's Christian elite was annihilated and the city became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Subdivisions of the Ottoman Empire">Ottoman province</a> (beylerbeylik) of <a href="/wiki/Rumelia" title="Rumelia">Rumelia</a> for more than four centuries. In the 16th century, Sofia's urban layout and appearance began to exhibit a clear Ottoman style.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia-oberbauer.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Sofia-oberbauer.png/220px-Sofia-oberbauer.png" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Sofia-oberbauer.png/330px-Sofia-oberbauer.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cc/Sofia-oberbauer.png 2x" data-file-width="392" data-file-height="278" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia-oberbauer.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sofia in mid-19th-century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There were fountains, <i><a href="/wiki/Turkish_bath" title="Turkish bath">hamams</a></i> (bathhouses), prominent churches such as <a href="/wiki/Saint_Sofia_Church,_Sofia" title="Saint Sofia Church, Sofia">Saint Sofia</a> were converted into mosques and in total there were 11 big and over 100 small mosques by the 17th century,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> of which only the <a href="/wiki/Banya_Bashi" class="mw-redirect" title="Banya Bashi">Banya Bashi</a> remains as a mosque today. During that time the town had a population of around 7,000.</p>
<p>The town was seized for several weeks by Bulgarian <i><a href="/wiki/Hajduk" title="Hajduk">hajduks</a></i> in 1599. In 1610 the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Vatican</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Sofia_and_Plovdiv" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Sofia and Plovdiv">See of Sofia</a> for Catholics of <a href="/wiki/Rumelia" title="Rumelia">Rumelia</a>, which existed until 1715 when most Catholics had emigrated.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The town was the center of Sofia <a href="/wiki/Eyalet" title="Eyalet">Eyalet</a> (1826‚Äì1864). <a href="/wiki/Nedelya_Petkova" title="Nedelya Petkova">Nedelya Petkova</a> created the first Bulgarian school for women in the city. The Ottomans hanged in Sofia the most honored <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarian</a> revolutionary of all time <a href="/wiki/Vasil_Levski" title="Vasil Levski">Levski</a> in 1873.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_and_contemporary_history">Modern and contemporary history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Modern and contemporary history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:376bombgroup-bulgaria-01-jun-1944.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/376bombgroup-bulgaria-01-jun-1944.gif/220px-376bombgroup-bulgaria-01-jun-1944.gif" width="220" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/376bombgroup-bulgaria-01-jun-1944.gif/330px-376bombgroup-bulgaria-01-jun-1944.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/376bombgroup-bulgaria-01-jun-1944.gif/440px-376bombgroup-bulgaria-01-jun-1944.gif 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="970" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:376bombgroup-bulgaria-01-jun-1944.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Sofia_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Sofia in World War II">allied bombing of Sofia in World War II</a> of Sofia in 1944</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877‚Äì1878)">Russo-Turkish War of 1877‚Äì78</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_Pasha_(Ottoman_general)" title="Suleiman Pasha (Ottoman general)">Suleiman Pasha</a> threatened to burn the city, until the foreign councils Leandre Legay, <a href="/wiki/Vito_Positano" title="Vito Positano">Vito Positano</a>, Rabbi Gabriel Almosnino and Josef Valdhart interceded for the city to be saved. However this saving did not apply to the Bulgarian citizens who faced executions.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Sofia was liberated (see <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sofia" title="Battle of Sofia">Battle of Sofia</a>) from <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_rule_of_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman rule of Bulgaria">Ottoman rule</a> by <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russian_Army" title="Imperial Russian Army">Russian forces</a> under Gen. <a href="/wiki/Iosif_Gurko" title="Iosif Gurko">Iosif Gurko</a> on 4 January 1878. It was proposed as a capital by <a href="/wiki/Marin_Drinov" title="Marin Drinov">Marin Drinov</a> and was accepted as such on 3 April 1879. By the time of its liberation the population of the city was 11,649.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most mosques in Sofia were destroyed in that war, seven of them destroyed in one night in December 1878 when a thunderstorm masked the noise of the explosions arranged by Russian military engineers.".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrampton2006114_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrampton2006114-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>For a few decades after the liberation, Sofia experienced large population growth, mainly from other regions of Bulgaria.</p>
<p>In 1900 the first electric lightbulb in the city was turned on.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Second_Balkan_War" title="Second Balkan War">Second Balkan War</a> Bulgaria was warring alone against five neighboring countries and the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian Army">Romanian Army</a> entered <a href="/wiki/Vrazhdebna" class="mw-redirect" title="Vrazhdebna">Vrazhdebna</a> in 1913, then a village seven miles (11 kilometres) from Sofia, now a suburb,<sup id="cite_ref-Hall97_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hall97-82">[82]</a></sup> which prompted Bulgaria to capitulate. During <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Bulgaria_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of Bulgaria during World War II">World War II in Bulgaria</a>, Bulgaria declared war on the US and UK on 13 December 1941 and in late 1943 and early 1944 <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Sofia_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Sofia in World War II">US and UK aircraft bombed Sofia</a>. As a consequence of the bombings around 2000 people were killed and thousands of buildings were destroyed or damaged including the Capital Library and thousands of books. In 1944 Sofia and the rest of Bulgaria was occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> and within days of the Soviet invasion Bulgaria declared war on Nazi Germany.</p>
<p>In 1925 a terrorist act of ultra-leftists failed their attempted assassination of the king but resulted in the destruction of a <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nedelya_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Nedelya Church">church</a> and many victims. It took 20 years to 1945 when the communist <a href="/wiki/Fatherland_Front_(Bulgaria)" title="Fatherland Front (Bulgaria)">Fatherland Front</a> took power and executed several thousand people. The transformations of Bulgaria into the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Bulgaria" title="People's Republic of Bulgaria">People's Republic of Bulgaria</a> in 1946 and into the Republic of Bulgaria in 1990 marked significant changes in the city's appearance. The population of Sofia expanded rapidly due to migration from the country. Whole new residential areas were built in the outskirts of the city, like Druzhba, Mladost and Lyulin. The <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Dimitrov_Mausoleum" title="Georgi Dimitrov Mausoleum">Georgi Dimitrov Mausoleum</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Dimitrov" title="Georgi Dimitrov">Dimitrov's</a> body had been preserved in a similar way to the <a href="/wiki/Lenin_mausoleum" class="mw-redirect" title="Lenin mausoleum">Lenin mausoleum</a>, was detonated in 1999.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Sofia_Boby_Dimitrov_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Downtown_Sofia_Boby_Dimitrov_1.jpg/220px-Downtown_Sofia_Boby_Dimitrov_1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Downtown_Sofia_Boby_Dimitrov_1.jpg/330px-Downtown_Sofia_Boby_Dimitrov_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Downtown_Sofia_Boby_Dimitrov_1.jpg/440px-Downtown_Sofia_Boby_Dimitrov_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Sofia_Boby_Dimitrov_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Diurnal view, including the <a href="/wiki/Largo,_Sofia" title="Largo, Sofia">Largo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky_Cathedral,_Sofia" title="Alexander Nevsky Cathedral, Sofia">Alexander Nevsky Cathedral</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Bulgaria)" title="National Assembly (Bulgaria)">National Assembly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sofia_University" title="Sofia University">Sofia University</a>, the building of <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_National_Television" title="Bulgarian National Television">BNT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ariana" title="Lake Ariana">Lake Ariana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borisova_gradina" title="Borisova gradina">Borisova gradina</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_from_above.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Sofia_from_above.jpg/220px-Sofia_from_above.jpg" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Sofia_from_above.jpg/330px-Sofia_from_above.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Sofia_from_above.jpg/440px-Sofia_from_above.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5137" data-file-height="2913" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_from_above.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nocturnal view of the city.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Sofia there are 607,473 dwellings and 101,696 buildings. According to modern records 39,551 dwellings were constructed until 1949, 119,943 between 1950 and 1969, 287,191 between 1970 and 1989, 57,916 in the 90s and 102,623 between 2000 and 2011. Until 1949, 13,114 buildings were constructed and between 10,000‚Äì20,000 in each following decade.<sup id="cite_ref-book_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-83">[83]</a></sup> Sofia's architecture combines a wide range of architectural styles, some of which are aesthetically incompatible. These vary from Christian Roman architecture and medieval Bulgar fortresses to Neoclassicism and prefabricated Socialist-era apartment blocks. A number of ancient Roman, Byzantine and medieval Bulgarian buildings are preserved in the centre of the city. These include the 4th century <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._George,_Sofia" title="Church of St. George, Sofia">Rotunda of St. George</a>, the walls of the Serdica fortress and the partially preserved <a href="/wiki/Amphitheatre_of_Serdica" title="Amphitheatre of Serdica">Amphitheatre of Serdica</a>.</p>
<p>After the Liberation War, knyaz <a href="/wiki/Alexander,_Prince_of_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexander, Prince of Bulgaria">Alexander Battenberg</a> invited architects from <a href="/wiki/Austria%E2%80%93Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Austria‚ÄìHungary">Austria‚ÄìHungary</a> to shape the new capital's architectural appearance.<sup id="cite_ref-Fig._Arts_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fig._Arts-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>Among the architects invited to work in Bulgaria were <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Gr%C3%BCnanger" title="Friedrich Gr√ºnanger">Friedrich Gr√ºnanger</a>, Adolf V√°clav Kol√°≈ô, and <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Rumpelmayer" title="Viktor Rumpelmayer">Viktor Rumpelmayer</a>, who designed the most important public buildings needed by the newly reestablished Bulgarian government, as well as numerous houses for the country's elite.<sup id="cite_ref-Fig._Arts_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fig._Arts-84">[84]</a></sup> Later, many foreign-educated Bulgarian architects also contributed. The architecture of Sofia's centre is thus a combination of <a href="/wiki/Baroque_Revival_architecture" title="Baroque Revival architecture">Neo-Baroque</a>, Neo-<a href="/wiki/Rococo" title="Rococo">Rococo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Revival_architecture" title="Renaissance Revival architecture">Neo-Renaissance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">Neoclassicism</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Secession" title="Vienna Secession">Vienna Secession</a> also later playing an important part, but it is mostly typically Central European.</p>
<p>After World War II and the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Communist_state" title="Communist state">Communist government</a> in Bulgaria in 1944, the architectural style was substantially altered. <a href="/wiki/Stalinist_architecture" title="Stalinist architecture">Stalinist Gothic</a> public buildings emerged in the centre, notably the spacious government complex around <a href="/wiki/Largo,_Sofia" title="Largo, Sofia">The Largo</a>, Vasil Levski Stadium, the Cyril and Methodius National Library and others. As the city grew outwards, the then-new neighbourhoods were dominated by many concrete <a href="/wiki/Tower_block" title="Tower block">tower blocks</a>, prefabricated panel apartment buildings and examples of <a href="/wiki/Brutalist_architecture" title="Brutalist architecture">Brutalist architecture</a>. They still make Sofia's housing very high compared to post-Western block countries,</p>
<p>After the abolition of <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">Communism</a> in 1989, Sofia witnessed the construction of whole business districts and neighbourhoods, as well as modern skryscraper-like glass-fronted office buildings, but also top-class residential neighbourhoods. The 126-metre (413&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Capital_Fort" title="Capital Fort">Capital Fort</a> Business Center will be the first skyscraper in Bulgaria, with 36 floors. However, the end of the old administration and centrally planned system also paved the way for chaotic and unrestrained construction, which continues today.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_areas">Green areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Green areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Borisova_gradina_autumn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Borisova_gradina_autumn.jpg/220px-Borisova_gradina_autumn.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Borisova_gradina_autumn.jpg/330px-Borisova_gradina_autumn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Borisova_gradina_autumn.jpg/440px-Borisova_gradina_autumn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="519" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Borisova_gradina_autumn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Borisova_gradina" title="Borisova gradina">Borisova gradina</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city has an extensive <a href="/wiki/Green_belt" title="Green belt">green belt</a>. Some of the neighbourhoods constructed after 2000 are densely built up and lack green spaces. There are four principal parks ‚Äì <a href="/wiki/Borisova_gradina" title="Borisova gradina">Borisova gradina</a> in the city centre and the <i>Southern</i>, <i>Western</i> and <i>Northern</i> parks. Several smaller parks, among which the Zaimov Park, <a href="/wiki/City_Garden_(Sofia)" title="City Garden (Sofia)">City Garden</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Doctors%27_Garden" title="Doctors' Garden">Doctors' Garden</a>, are located in central Sofia. The <a href="/wiki/Vitosha" title="Vitosha">Vitosha Nature Park</a> (the oldest <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national park</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> includes most of <a href="/wiki/Vitosha" title="Vitosha">Vitosha mountain</a> and covers an area of 266 square kilometres (103&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> with roughly half of it lying within the municipality of Sofia. Vitosha Mountain is a popular hiking destination due to its proximity and ease of access via car and public transport. Two functioning cable cars provide year long access from the outskirts of the city. The mountain offers favorable skiing conditions during the winter when multiple ski slopes of various difficulty are made available. Access to the ski slopes is regulated, they are maintained daily and health and safety personnel is available to assist in case of injury. Skiing passes typically allow unlimited access to the ski slopes, cable cars and other transport facilities. Skiing equipment can be rented and skiing lessons are available.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_law">Government and law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Government and law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>Sofia as a capital is the location of all Bulgarian state authorities ‚Äì <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legislative" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative">legislative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a>, the headquarters of all parties and the delegation of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>. This includes the Parliament, the Presidency, the Council of Ministers and all the ministries, <a href="/wiki/Supreme_court" title="Supreme court">supreme courts</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Bulgaria" title="Constitutional Court of Bulgaria">Constitutional Court of Bulgaria</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sofia_Capital_Municipality" title="Sofia Capital Municipality">Sofia Municipality</a> is identical to <a href="/wiki/Sofia_City_Province" title="Sofia City Province">Sofia City Province</a>, which is distinct from <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Province" title="Sofia Province">Sofia Province</a>, which surrounds but does not include the capital itself. Besides the city proper, the 24 districts of Sofia Municipality encompass three other towns and 34 villages.<sup id="cite_ref-District_Mayors_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-District_Mayors-91">[91]</a></sup> Districts and settlements have their own governor who is elected in a popular election. The assembly members are chosen every four years. The common head of Sofia Municipality and all the 38 settlements is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Sofia" title="List of mayors of Sofia">mayor of Sofia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-District_Mayors_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-District_Mayors-91">[91]</a></sup> The current mayor <a href="/wiki/Yordanka_Fandakova" title="Yordanka Fandakova">Yordanka Fandakova</a> is serving a third consecutive term, having won the 2015 election at first round with 238,500 votes,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> or 60.2% of the vote, when <a href="/wiki/Reformist_Bloc" title="Reformist Bloc">Reformist Bloc</a> opponent Vili Lilkov was second with 9.6%; the turnout was 41.25%.<sup id="cite_ref-2015e_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015e-93">[93]</a></sup> Some party leaders claimed that ballots were falsified and called for annulment of the election.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> A precedent happened, due to the suspicion, as a preventative action between 300 and 5000 people and counters had been locked inside <a href="/wiki/Arena_Armeets" class="mw-redirect" title="Arena Armeets">Arena Armeets</a> against their will for two days,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> following which the director of the Electoral Commission of Sofia resigned at the request of Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Boyko_Borissov" title="Boyko Borissov">Boyko Borissov</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The number one problem that mayor <a href="/wiki/Yordanka_Fandakova" title="Yordanka Fandakova">Yordanka Fandakova</a> acknowledges and is working on is the <a href="/wiki/Street_dogs_in_Sofia" title="Street dogs in Sofia">street dogs in Sofia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Although according to officials Sofia hosts 6600 street dogs currently, unofficially there at between 35,000 and 70,000 stray dogs.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> They have become part of urban life in Sofia, but the problem spotted into light after a pack mauled a prominent <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> professor to death in 2012, who was the president of the <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">Wall Street</a> Investment Bank and worked for the <a href="/wiki/US_Department_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="US Department of State">US Department of State</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
