</div>
</div>
<p>With a murder rate of 1.8/per 100.000 people (as of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>) Sofia is a quite safe capital city.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Nevertheless, in the 21st century, crimes, including <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_mafia" title="Bulgarian mafia">Bulgarian mafia</a> killings, caused problems in the city,<sup id="cite_ref-CoulbyCowen2013_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CoulbyCowen2013-104">[104]</a></sup> where authorities had difficulties convicting the authors,<sup id="cite_ref-Noutcheva2012_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Noutcheva2012-105">[105]</a></sup> which had caused the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> to warn the Bulgarian government that the country would not be able to join the EU unless it curbed crime<sup id="cite_ref-Economist_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist-106">[106]</a></sup> (Bulgaria eventually joined in 2007).<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Many of the most severe crimes are <a href="/wiki/Contract_killings" class="mw-redirect" title="Contract killings">contract killings</a> connected to the <a href="/wiki/Organized_crime" title="Organized crime">organized crime</a>, but these had dropped in recent years after several arrests of gang members.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Bulgaria#Corruption" title="Crime in Bulgaria">Corruption in Bulgaria</a> also affects Sofia'a authorities. According to the director of Sofia District Police Directorate the largest share of the crimes are <a href="/wiki/Theft" title="Theft">thefts</a>, making up 62.4% of all crimes in the capital city. Increasing are <a href="/wiki/Fraud" title="Fraud">frauds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drug" title="Drug">drug</a>-related crimes, <a href="/wiki/Petty_theft" class="mw-redirect" title="Petty theft">petty theft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vandalism" title="Vandalism">vandalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> According to a survey, almost a third of Sofia's residents say that they never feel safe in the Bulgarian capital, while 20% always feel safe.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the consumer-reported perceived crime risk on the <a href="/wiki/Numbeo" title="Numbeo">Numbeo</a> database was "high" for theft and vandalism and "low" for violent crimes; safety while walking during daylight was rated "very high", and "moderate" during the night.<sup id="cite_ref-Numbeo_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Numbeo-111">[111]</a></sup> With 1,600 prisoners the <a href="/wiki/Incarceration_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Incarceration rate">incarceration rate</a> is above 0.1%;<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> however, roughly 70% of all prisoners are part of the <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Bulgaria" title="Romani people in Bulgaria">Romani minority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tourist_attractions_in_Sofia" title="Tourist attractions in Sofia">Tourist attractions in Sofia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_churches_in_Sofia" title="List of churches in Sofia">List of churches in Sofia</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_entertainment">Arts and entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Arts and entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ivan_Vazov_National_Theatre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Ivan_Vazov_National_Theatre.jpg/250px-Ivan_Vazov_National_Theatre.jpg" width="250" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Ivan_Vazov_National_Theatre.jpg/375px-Ivan_Vazov_National_Theatre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Ivan_Vazov_National_Theatre.jpg/500px-Ivan_Vazov_National_Theatre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1152" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ivan_Vazov_National_Theatre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Vazov_National_Theatre" title="Ivan Vazov National Theatre">Ivan Vazov National Theatre</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sofia concentrates the majority of Bulgaria's leading performing arts troupes. Theatre is by far the most popular form of performing art, and theatrical venues are among the most visited, second only to cinemas. The oldest such institution is the <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Vazov_National_Theatre" title="Ivan Vazov National Theatre">Ivan Vazov National Theatre</a>, which performs mainly classical plays and is situated in the very centre of the city.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Opera_and_Ballet_of_Bulgaria" title="National Opera and Ballet of Bulgaria">National Opera and Ballet of Bulgaria</a> is a combined <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ballet" title="Ballet">ballet</a> collective, established in 1891. However, it did not begin performances on a regular basis until 1909. Some of Bulgaria's most famous operatic singers, such as <a href="/wiki/Nicolai_Ghiaurov" title="Nicolai Ghiaurov">Nicolai Ghiaurov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghena_Dimitrova" title="Ghena Dimitrova">Ghena Dimitrova</a>, have made their first appearances on the stage of the National Opera and Ballet. The <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_of_Culture" title="National Palace of Culture">National Palace of Culture</a> regularly hold classical concerts. Bulgaria's largest art museums are located in the central areas of the city. Two emblematic galleries in Sofia ‚Äì the <a href="/wiki/National_Art_Gallery_(Bulgaria)" title="National Art Gallery (Bulgaria)">National Art Gallery</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_for_Foreign_Art" title="National Gallery for Foreign Art">National Gallery for Foreign Art</a> united their collections in a new structure. Seven Ministers of Culture have worked on this project over the years. The project, also known as the Bulgarian Louvre, gathered under one roof a host of Bulgarian, European, American, Asian and African works of art. Nearly two thousand works created by artists from Bulgaria and abroad are on display in twenty eight exhibition halls. Following a special competition, the art collection was named National Gallery Square 500 <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://bnr.bg/en/post/100561824/national-gallery-square-500-the-non-standard-museum">(source)</a>. Its collections encompass diverse cultural items such as <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Empire" title="Ashanti Empire">Ashanti Empire</a> sculptures, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> art, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a> painting, works by <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_D%C3%BCrer" title="Albrecht D√ºrer">Albrecht D√ºrer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Greuze" title="Jean-Baptiste Greuze">Jean-Baptiste Greuze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Auguste_Rodin" title="Auguste Rodin">Auguste Rodin</a>, among others. The <a href="/wiki/Crypt" title="Crypt">crypt</a> of the Alexander Nevsky cathedral holds a collection of Eastern Orthodox icons from the 9th to the 19th century. Other museums are the <a href="/wiki/National_Historical_Museum_(Bulgaria)" title="National Historical Museum (Bulgaria)">National Historical Museum</a> with a collection of more than 600,000 items; the <a href="/wiki/National_Polytechnical_Museum" title="National Polytechnical Museum">National Polytechnical Museum</a> with more than 1,000 technological items on display; the <a href="/wiki/National_Archaeological_Museum_(Bulgaria)" title="National Archaeological Museum (Bulgaria)">National Archaeological Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Natural_History_(Bulgaria)" title="National Museum of Natural History (Bulgaria)">Museum of Natural History</a>. The <a href="/wiki/SS._Cyril_and_Methodius_National_Library" title="SS. Cyril and Methodius National Library">SS. Cyril and Methodius National Library</a> houses the largest national collection of books and documents (1,714,211 books and some 6 million other documents)<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> and is Bulgaria's oldest cultural institute. The <a href="/wiki/Boyana_Church" title="Boyana Church">Boyana Church</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> World Heritage site, contains realistic frescoes, depicting more than 240 human images and a total 89 scenes, were painted. With their vital, humanistic realism they are a <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> phenomenon at its culmination phase in the context of the common-European art.<sup id="cite_ref-ecker_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecker-115">[115]</a></sup> Muzeiko is a new museum opened in 2015. It is a space with over 130 interactive games created for children and curious adults. The entire content of the museum is designed to inspire children to learn, discover and explore the sciences, while helping children, their families and educators spend time together actively and effectively.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vitosha_Blvd._2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Vitosha_Blvd._2.jpg/250px-Vitosha_Blvd._2.jpg" width="250" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Vitosha_Blvd._2.jpg/375px-Vitosha_Blvd._2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Vitosha_Blvd._2.jpg/500px-Vitosha_Blvd._2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1152" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vitosha_Blvd._2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Vitosha_Boulevard" title="Vitosha Boulevard">Vitosha Blvd.</a>, the main shopping street in the city.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cinema is the most popular form of entertainment. In recent years, cinematic venues have been concentrated in trade centres and <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">malls</a>, and independent halls have been closed. <a href="/wiki/Mall_of_Sofia" title="Mall of Sofia">Mall of Sofia</a> holds one of the largest <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> cinemas in Europe. Most films are American productions, although European and domestic films are increasingly shown. <i>Odeon</i> (not part of the <a href="/wiki/Odeon_Cinemas" title="Odeon Cinemas">Odeon Cinemas</a> chain) shows exclusively European and independent American films, as well as 20th century classics. Bulgaria's once thriving film industry, concentrated in the <a href="/wiki/Boyana_Film" class="mw-redirect" title="Boyana Film">Boyana Film</a> studios, has suffered a period of decay after 1990. A relative revival of the industry began after 2001. After the acquisition of Boyana Film by <a href="/wiki/Nu_Image" title="Nu Image">Nu Image</a>, several moderately successful productions have been shot in and around Sofia, such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Contract_(2006_film)" title="The Contract (2006 film)">The Contract</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Black_Dahlia_(film)" title="The Black Dahlia (film)">The Black Dahlia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hitman_(2007_film)" title="Hitman (2007 film)">Hitman</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Conan_the_Barbarian_(2011_film)" title="Conan the Barbarian (2011 film)">Conan the Barbarian</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Spartacus_(miniseries)" title="Spartacus (miniseries)">Spartacus</a></i>. The Nu Boyana Film studios have also hosted some of the scenes for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Expendables_2" title="The Expendables 2">The Expendables 2</a></i>.</p>
<p>The city houses many cultural institutes such as the Russian Cultural Institute, the Polish Cultural Institute, the Hungarian Institute, the Czech and the Slovak Cultural Institutes, the Italian Cultural Institute, the French Cultural Institute, <a href="/wiki/Goethe-Institut" title="Goethe-Institut">Goethe Institut</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Council" title="British Council">British Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Cervantes" title="Instituto Cervantes">Instituto Cervantes</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Open_Society_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Society Institute">Open Society Institute</a>, which regularly organise temporary expositions of visual, sound and literary works by artists from their respective countries.</p>
<p>Some of the biggest telecommunications companies, TV and radio stations, newspapers, magazines, and web portals are based in Sofia, including the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_National_Television" title="Bulgarian National Television">Bulgarian National Television</a>, <a href="/wiki/BTV_(Bulgaria)" title="BTV (Bulgaria)">bTV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nova_Television_(Bulgaria)" class="mw-redirect" title="Nova Television (Bulgaria)">Nova TV</a>. Top-circulation newspapers include <i><a href="/wiki/24_Chasa" title="24 Chasa">24 Chasa</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dneven_Trud" class="mw-redirect" title="Dneven Trud">Trud</a></i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexander_Nevsky,_Sofia_-_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Alexander_Nevsky%2C_Sofia_-_01.JPG/250px-Alexander_Nevsky%2C_Sofia_-_01.JPG" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Alexander_Nevsky%2C_Sofia_-_01.JPG/375px-Alexander_Nevsky%2C_Sofia_-_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Alexander_Nevsky%2C_Sofia_-_01.JPG/500px-Alexander_Nevsky%2C_Sofia_-_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3672" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexander_Nevsky,_Sofia_-_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky_Cathedral,_Sofia" title="Alexander Nevsky Cathedral, Sofia">St. Alexander Nevsky Cathedral</a>, one of the largest Eastern Orthodox cathedrals in the world.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sofia is one of the most visited tourist destinations in Bulgaria alongside coastal and mountain resorts. Among its highlights is the <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky_Cathedral,_Sofia" title="Alexander Nevsky Cathedral, Sofia">Alexander Nevsky Cathedral</a>, one of the symbols of Bulgaria, constructed in the late 19th century. It occupies an area of 3,170 square metres (34,122 square feet) and can hold 10,000 people.</p>
<p>Sofia holds Bulgaria's largest <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://visitmybulgaria.com/destination/museums-in-bulgaria/">museum</a> collections, which attract tourists and students for practical studies. The <a href="/wiki/National_Historical_Museum_(Bulgaria)" title="National Historical Museum (Bulgaria)">National Historical Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Boyana" title="Boyana">Boyana</a> district has a vast collection of more than 650,000 historical items dating from Prehistory to the modern era, although only 10,000 of them are permanently displayed due to the lack of space.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Smaller collections of items related mostly to the history of Sofia are in the <a href="/wiki/National_Archaeological_Museum_(Bulgaria)" title="National Archaeological Museum (Bulgaria)">National Archaeological Museum</a>, a former mosque located between the edifices of the National Bank and the Presidency. Two natural sciences museums ‚Äî the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Natural_History_(Bulgaria)" title="National Museum of Natural History (Bulgaria)">Natural History Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Earth_and_Man_National_Museum" title="Earth and Man National Museum">Earth and Man</a> ‚Äî display minerals, animal species (alive and <a href="/wiki/Taxidermy" title="Taxidermy">taxidermic</a>) and rare materials. The Ethnographic Museum and the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Military_History_(Bulgaria)" title="National Museum of Military History (Bulgaria)">National Museum of Military History</a> are other places of interest, holding large collections of Bulgarian folk costumes and armaments, respectively.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Vitosha_Boulevard" title="Vitosha Boulevard">Vitosha Boulevard</a>, also called <i>Vitoshka</i>, is a pedestrian zone with numerous cafes, restaurants, fashion boutiques, and <a href="/wiki/Luxury_good" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxury good">luxury goods</a> stores. Sofia's <a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">geographic location</a>, in the foothills of the weekend retreat <a href="/wiki/Vitosha" title="Vitosha">Vitosha</a> mountain, further adds to the city's specific atmosphere.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%90%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%B5%D1%86_%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/%D0%90%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%90%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%B5%D1%86_%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg/250px-%D0%90%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%90%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%B5%D1%86_%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg" width="250" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/%D0%90%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%90%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%B5%D1%86_%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg/375px-%D0%90%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%90%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%B5%D1%86_%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/%D0%90%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%90%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%B5%D1%86_%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg/500px-%D0%90%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%90%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%B5%D1%86_%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2200" data-file-height="1464" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%90%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%B5%D1%86_%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The interior of <a href="/wiki/Arena_Armeets" class="mw-redirect" title="Arena Armeets">Arena Armeets</a>, a multi-purpose indoor arena.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A large number of sports clubs are based in the city. During the Communist era most sports clubs concentrated on all-round sporting development, therefore <a href="/wiki/PFC_CSKA_Sofia" title="PFC CSKA Sofia">CSKA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Levski_Sofia_(sports_club)" title="Levski Sofia (sports club)">Levski</a>, <a href="/wiki/PFC_Lokomotiv_Sofia" title="PFC Lokomotiv Sofia">Lokomotiv</a> and <a href="/wiki/PFC_Slavia_Sofia" title="PFC Slavia Sofia">Slavia</a> are dominant not only in football, but in many other team sports as well. Basketball and volleyball also have strong traditions in Sofia. A notable local <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball team</a> is twice <a href="/wiki/Euroleague#Champions_1958-2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Euroleague">European Champions Cup</a> finalist <a href="/wiki/PBC_Lukoil_Academic" class="mw-redirect" title="PBC Lukoil Academic">Lukoil Akademik</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Volleyball_Federation" title="Bulgarian Volleyball Federation">Bulgarian Volleyball Federation</a> is the world's second-oldest, and it was an exhibition tournament organised by the BVF in Sofia that convinced the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> to include volleyball as an <a href="/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_Summer_Olympics#History" title="Volleyball at the Summer Olympics">olympic sport</a> in 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Tennis is increasingly popular in the city. Currently there are some ten<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tennis_court" title="Tennis court">tennis court</a> complexes within the city including the one founded by former <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Tennis_Association" title="Women's Tennis Association">WTA</a> top-ten athlete <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_Maleeva" title="Magdalena Maleeva">Magdalena Maleeva</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sofia applied to host the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympic Games</a> in 1992 and in 1994, coming 2nd and 3rd respectively. The city was also an applicant for the <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">2014 Winter Olympics</a>, but was not selected as candidate. In addition, Sofia hosted <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket_1957" title="EuroBasket 1957">Eurobasket 1957</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1961_Summer_Universiade" title="1961 Summer Universiade">1961</a> and <a href="/wiki/1977_Summer_Universiade" title="1977 Summer Universiade">1977 Summer Universiades</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/1983_Winter_Universiade" title="1983 Winter Universiade">1983</a> and <a href="/wiki/1989_Winter_Universiade" title="1989 Winter Universiade">1989 winter editions</a>. In 2012, it hosted the <a href="/wiki/FIVB_World_League" class="mw-redirect" title="FIVB World League">FIVB World League</a> finals.</p>
<p>The city is home to a number of large sports venues, including the 43,000-seat <a href="/wiki/Vasil_Levski_National_Stadium" title="Vasil Levski National Stadium">Vasil Levski National Stadium</a> which hosts international football matches, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Asparuhov_Stadium" title="Georgi Asparuhov Stadium">Georgi Asparuhov Stadium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lokomotiv_Stadium_(Sofia)" title="Lokomotiv Stadium (Sofia)">Lokomotiv Stadium</a>, the main venues for outdoor musical concerts. <a href="/wiki/Armeets_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Armeets Arena">Armeets Arena</a> holds many indoor events and has a capacity of up to 19,000 people depending on its use. The venue was inaugurated on July 30, 2011, and the first event it hosted was a friendly volleyball match between Bulgaria and Serbia. There are two <a href="/wiki/Ice_skating" title="Ice skating">ice skating</a> complexes&#160;‚Äî the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Sports_Palace" title="Winter Sports Palace">Winter Sports Palace</a> with a capacity of 4,600 and the Slavia Winter Stadium with a capacity of 2,000, both containing two rinks each.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Velodrome" title="Velodrome">velodrome</a> with 5,000 seats in the city's <a href="/wiki/Borisova_gradina" title="Borisova gradina">central park</a> is currently undergoing renovation.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> There are also various other sports complexes in the city which belong to institutions other than football clubs, such as those of the <a href="/wiki/National_Sports_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="National Sports Academy">National Sports Academy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Bulgarian Academy of Sciences">Bulgarian Academy of Sciences</a>, or those of different universities. There are more than fifteen swimming complexes in the city, most of them outdoor.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Nearly all of these were constructed as competition venues and therefore have seating facilities for several hundred people.</p>
<p>There are two <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf courses</a> just to the east of Sofia&#160;‚Äî in <a href="/wiki/Elin_Pelin" title="Elin Pelin">Elin Pelin</a> (St Sofia club) and in <a href="/wiki/Ihtiman" title="Ihtiman">Ihtiman</a> (Air Sofia club), and a horseriding club (St George club).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Population growth over the years (in thousands):</b></p>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_d35aac81af16e585643272c35b3e2e23" id="timeline_d35aac81af16e585643272c35b3e2e23"></map><img usemap="#timeline_d35aac81af16e585643272c35b3e2e23" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/d35aac81af16e585643272c35b3e2e23.png" /></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:13.modelat_bay_Georgi_i_studenti_ot_akademiata.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/13.modelat_bay_Georgi_i_studenti_ot_akademiata.jpg/220px-13.modelat_bay_Georgi_i_studenti_ot_akademiata.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/13.modelat_bay_Georgi_i_studenti_ot_akademiata.jpg/330px-13.modelat_bay_Georgi_i_studenti_ot_akademiata.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/13.modelat_bay_Georgi_i_studenti_ot_akademiata.jpg/440px-13.modelat_bay_Georgi_i_studenti_ot_akademiata.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1886" data-file-height="1289" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:13.modelat_bay_Georgi_i_studenti_ot_akademiata.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Students of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Arts" title="National Academy of Arts">National Academy of Arts</a> (circa 1952‚Äì53). People aged 20‚Äì25 years have been the most numerous group in the city since the process of Bulgarian urbanization.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to 2016 data, the city has a population of 1,304,772 and the whole <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Capital_Municipality" title="Sofia Capital Municipality">Sofia Capital Municipality</a> of 1,441,918.<sup id="cite_ref-nsi.bg_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsi.bg-9">[9]</a></sup> The first census carried out in February 1878 by the Russian Army recorded a population of 11,694 inhabitants including 6,560 <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a>, 3,538 <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian Jews">Jews</a>, 839 <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a> and 737 <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a>.</p>
<p>The ratio of women per 1,000 men was 1,102. The <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> per 1000 people was 12.3 per mille and steadily increasing in the last 5 years, the <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">death rate</a> reaching 12.1 per mille and decreasing. The natural growth rate during 2009 was 0.2 per mille, the first positive growth rate in nearly 20 years. The considerable immigration to the capital from poorer regions of the country, as well as urbanisation, are among the other reasons for the increase in Sofia's population. The <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality rate</a> was 5.6 per 1,000, down from 18.9 in 1980. According to the 2011 census, people aged 20‚Äì24 years are the most numerous group, numbering 133,170 individuals and accounting for 11% of the total 1,202,761 people. The median age is 38 though. According to the census, 1,056,738 citizens (87.9%) are recorded as ethnic <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a>, 17,550 (1.5%) as <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Bulgaria" title="Romani people in Bulgaria">Romani</a>, 6,149 (0.5%) as <a href="/wiki/Turks_in_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Turks in Bulgaria">Turks</a>, 9,569 (0.8%) belonged to other ethnic groups, 6,993 (0.6%) do not self-identify and 105,762 (8.8%) remained with undeclared affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> This statistic should not necessarily be taken at face value due to conflicting data&#160;‚Äì such as for the predominantly Roma neighbourhood of Fakulteta, which alone may have a population of 45,000.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the 2011 census, throughout the whole municipality some 892,511 people (69.1%) are recorded as <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox">Eastern Orthodox</a> <a href="/wiki/Christians" class="mw-redirect" title="Christians">Christians</a>, 10,256 (0.8%) as <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Bulgaria" title="Protestantism in Bulgaria">Protestant</a>, 6,767 (0.5%) as <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Bulgaria" title="Islam in Bulgaria">Muslim</a>, 5,572 (0.4%) as <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Bulgaria" title="Roman Catholicism in Bulgaria">Roman Catholic</a>, 4,010 (0.3%) belonged to other faith and 372,475 (28.8%) declared themselves <a href="/wiki/Irreligious" class="mw-redirect" title="Irreligious">irreligious</a> or did not mention any faith. The data says that roughly a third of the total population have already earned a <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> degree. Of the population aged 15‚Äì64 ‚Äì 265,248 people within the municipality (28.5%) are not economically active, the unemployed being another group of 55,553 people (6%), a large share of whom have completed <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a>. The largest group are occupied in <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">trading</a>, followed by those in <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Manufacturing industry">manufacturing industry</a>. Within the municipality, three quarters, or 965,328 people are recorded as having access to <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">television</a> at home and 836,435 (64.8%) as having <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">internet</a>. Out of 464,865 homes ‚Äì 432,847 have connection to the communal <a href="/wiki/Sanitary_sewer" title="Sanitary sewer">sanitary sewer</a>, while 2,732 do not have any. Of these 864 do not have any <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">water supply</a> and 688 have other than communal. Over 99.6% of males and females aged over 9 are recorded as <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literate</a>. The largest group of the population aged over 20 are recorded to live within <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">marriage</a> (46.3%), another 43.8% are recorded as single and another 9.9% as having other type of coexistence/partnership, whereas not married in total are a majority and among people aged up to 40 and over 70. The people with juridical status <a href="/wiki/Divorce" title="Divorce">divorced</a> or <a href="/wiki/Widow" title="Widow">widowed</a> are either part of the factual singles or those having another type of partnership, each of the two constitutes by around 10% of the population aged over 20. Only over 1% of the juridically married do not de facto live within marriage. The families that consist of two people are 46.8%, another 34.2% of the families are made up by three people, whereas most of the households (36.5%) consist of only one person.<sup id="cite_ref-book_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sofia was declared the national capital in 1879. One year later, in 1880, it was the fifth-largest city in the country after <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv" title="Plovdiv">Plovdiv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Varna" title="Varna">Varna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruse,_Bulgaria" title="Ruse, Bulgaria">Ruse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shumen" title="Shumen">Shumen</a>. Plovdiv remained the most populous Bulgarian town until 1892 when Sofia took the lead. The city is the hot spot of internal migration, the capital population is increasing and is around 17% of the national,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> thus a small number of people with local roots remain today, they dominate the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Sofia" title="Districts of Sofia">rural suburbs</a> and are called <a href="/wiki/Shopi" title="Shopi">Shopi</a>. Shopi speak one of the transitional <a href="/wiki/South_Slavic_languages" title="South Slavic languages">South Slavic</a> dialects, along with <a href="/wiki/Torlakian_dialect" title="Torlakian dialect">Torlakian</a>, sharing features with both eastern (<a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>) and western (<a href="/wiki/Serbocroatian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbocroatian language">Serbo-Croatian</a>) branches,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> although they are given non-Slavic origin through the ancient Thracian <a href="/wiki/Serdi" title="Serdi">Serdi</a>, the founders of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zx620y348_2628889.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Zx620y348_2628889.png/250px-Zx620y348_2628889.png" width="250" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Zx620y348_2628889.png/375px-Zx620y348_2628889.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/09/Zx620y348_2628889.png 2x" data-file-width="419" data-file-height="252" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zx620y348_2628889.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Capital_Fort" title="Capital Fort">Capital Fort</a>, the 126-meter skyscraper near <a href="/wiki/Tsarigradsko_shose" title="Tsarigradsko shose">Tsarigradsko shose</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sofia is the economic heart of Bulgaria and home to most major Bulgarian and international companies operating in the country, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_National_Bank" title="Bulgarian National Bank">Bulgarian National Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Stock_Exchange_%E2%80%93_Sofia" title="Bulgarian Stock Exchange ‚Äì Sofia">Bulgarian Stock Exchange</a>. The city's GDP PPS per capita at current market prices stood at ‚Ç¨26,600<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> in 2012, which was 100% of the then EU average, according to Eurostat data ‚Äì well above the same year's national average of 46%. The city and its surrounding <a href="/wiki/Yugozapaden" class="mw-redirect" title="Yugozapaden">Yugozapaden</a> NUTS II planning region had a per capita PPS GDP of ‚Ç¨20,600<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> in 2014, higher than any other region in the country. In 2008, the average per capita annual income was 4,572 leva ($3,479).<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> For the same year, the strongest sectors of the city's economy in terms of annual production were manufacturing ($5.5 bln.), metallurgy ($1.84 bln.), electricity, gas and water supply ($1.6 bln.) and food and beverages ($778 mln.).<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Economic output in 2011 amounted to 15.9 billion leva, or $11.04 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-NSI_regional_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSI_regional-132">[132]</a></sup> The average monthly gross wages paid in December 2015 amount to ‚Ç¨645, the highest in Bulgaria and the lowest among EU capitals.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a> listed Sofia as one of the top 10 places in the world to launch a startup business, because of the low corporate tax (10%), the extremely fast internet connection speed available ‚Äì one of the fastest in the world, and the presence of several investment funds, including Eleven Startup Accelerator, LAUNCHub and Neveq.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>Historically, after World War II and the era of industrialisation under socialism, the city and its surrounding areas expanded rapidly and became the most heavily industrialised region of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Face_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Face-135">[135]</a></sup> The influx of workers from other parts of the country became so intense that a restriction policy was imposed, and residing in the capital was only possible after obtaining Sofianite citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-Face_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Face-135">[135]</a></sup> However, after the political changes in 1989, this kind of citizenship was removed.</p>
<p>Increasingly, Sofia is becoming an <a href="/wiki/Outsourcing" title="Outsourcing">outsourcing</a> destination for <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational companies</a>, among them <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a>, <a href="/wiki/SAP_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="SAP AG">SAP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Software_AG" title="Software AG">Software AG</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_Air" title="Bulgaria Air">Bulgaria Air</a>, PPD, the national airline of Bulgaria, has its head office on the grounds of <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Airport" title="Sofia Airport">Sofia Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> From 2007 to 2011, the city attracted a cumulative total of $11.6 billion in <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NSI_regional_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSI_regional-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>Up until 2007 Sofia experienced rapid <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">economic growth</a>. In 2008, apartment prices increased dramatically, with a growth rate of 30%.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> In 2009, prices fell by 26%.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2015 Sofia was ranked 30th out of 300 global cities in terms of combined growth in employment and real gross domestic product (GDP) per capita in 2013‚Äì2014. This was the highest rank amongst cities in Southeast Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> The real GDP (PPP) per capita growth was 2.5% to $33,105 (28,456 euro) and the employment went up by 3.4% to 962,400 in 2013‚Äì2014.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_and_infrastructure">Transport and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transport and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_metro_at_Musagenitsa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Sofia_metro_at_Musagenitsa.jpg/220px-Sofia_metro_at_Musagenitsa.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Sofia_metro_at_Musagenitsa.jpg/330px-Sofia_metro_at_Musagenitsa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Sofia_metro_at_Musagenitsa.jpg/440px-Sofia_metro_at_Musagenitsa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_metro_at_Musagenitsa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sofia_Metro" title="Sofia Metro">Sofia Metro</a> train at <a href="/wiki/Musagenitsa_Metro_Station" title="Musagenitsa Metro Station">Musagenitsa Metro Station</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With its developing infrastructure and strategic location, Sofia is a major hub for international railway and automobile transport. Three of the ten <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_corridors" title="Pan-European corridors">Pan-European Transport Corridors</a> cross the city: <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_Corridor_IV" title="Pan-European Corridor IV">IV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_Corridor_VIII" title="Pan-European Corridor VIII">VIII</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_Corridor_X" title="Pan-European Corridor X">X</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-infrastructure_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infrastructure-142">[142]</a></sup> All major types of transport (except <a href="/wiki/Ship_transport" title="Ship transport">water</a>) are represented in the city. The <a href="/wiki/Central_Railway_Station,_Sofia" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Railway Station, Sofia">Central Railway Station</a> is the primary hub for domestic and international rail transport. Sofia has 186&#160;km (116 miles) of railway lines.<sup id="cite_ref-NSI_regional_132-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSI_regional-132">[132]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Airport" title="Sofia Airport">Sofia Airport</a> handled 3,815,158 passengers in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sofia_Public_Transport" title="Sofia Public Transport">Public transport</a> is well-developed with <a href="/wiki/Public_buses_in_Sofia" title="Public buses in Sofia">bus</a> (2,380&#160;km (1,479&#160;mi) network),<sup id="cite_ref-bus_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bus-144">[144]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sofia_tram_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Sofia tram system">tram</a> (308&#160;km (191&#160;mi)) network,<sup id="cite_ref-tramway_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tramway-145">[145]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Sofia" title="Trolleybuses in Sofia">trolleybus</a> (193&#160;km (120&#160;mi) network),<sup id="cite_ref-trolleybuses_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trolleybuses-146">[146]</a></sup> lines running in all areas of the city,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> although some of the vehicles are in a poor condition. The <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Metro" title="Sofia Metro">Sofia Metro</a> became operational in 1998, and now has two lines and 34 stations.<sup id="cite_ref-subway2_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-subway2-149">[149]</a></sup> As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the system has 39&#160;km (24&#160;mi) of track. Six new stations were opened in 2009, two more in April 2012, and eleven more in August 2012. Construction works on the extension of the first line are underway and it is expected to reach the airport by 2014. A third line is currently in the late stages of planning and it is expected that its construction starts in 2014. This line will complete the proposed subway system of three lines with about 65&#160;km (40&#160;mi) of lines.<sup id="cite_ref-subway_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-subway-150">[150]</a></sup> The master plan for the Sofia Metro includes three lines with a total of 63 stations.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> In recent years the <a href="/wiki/Marshrutka" title="Marshrutka">marshrutka</a>, a private passenger van, began serving fixed routes and proved an efficient and popular <a href="/wiki/Mode_of_transport" title="Mode of transport">means of transport</a> by being faster than public transport but cheaper than taxis. As of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> these vans numbered 368 and serviced 48 lines around the city and suburbs.<sup id="cite_ref-infrastructure_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infrastructure-142">[142]</a></sup> There are around 13,000 <a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">taxi cabs</a> operating in the <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">city</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> Low fares in comparison with other European countries, make taxis affordable and popular among a big part of the city population.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Road_junction_@_Sitnyakovo_blvd,_Sofia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Road_junction_%40_Sitnyakovo_blvd%2C_Sofia.jpg/230px-Road_junction_%40_Sitnyakovo_blvd%2C_Sofia.jpg" width="230" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Road_junction_%40_Sitnyakovo_blvd%2C_Sofia.jpg/345px-Road_junction_%40_Sitnyakovo_blvd%2C_Sofia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Road_junction_%40_Sitnyakovo_blvd%2C_Sofia.jpg/460px-Road_junction_%40_Sitnyakovo_blvd%2C_Sofia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1063" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Road_junction_@_Sitnyakovo_blvd,_Sofia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tsarigradsko_shose" title="Tsarigradsko shose">Tsarigradsko shose</a>, one of the busiest boulevards in Sofia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Private automobile ownership has grown rapidly in the 1990s; more than 1,000,000 cars were registered in Sofia after 2002. The city has the 4th-highest number of automobiles per capita in the European Union at 546.4 vehicles per 1,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> The municipality was known for minor and cosmetic repairs and many streets are in a poor condition. This is noticeably changing in the past years. There are different boulevards and streets in the city with a higher amount of traffic than others. These include Tsarigradsko shose, Cherni Vrah, Bulgaria, Slivnitsa and Todor Aleksandrov boulevards, as well as the city's ring road, where long chains of cars are formed at peak hours and <a href="/wiki/Traffic_jam" class="mw-redirect" title="Traffic jam">traffic jams</a> occur regularly.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> Consequently, traffic and <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a> problems have become more severe and receive regular criticism in local media. The extension of the underground system is hoped to alleviate the city's immense traffic problems.</p>
<p>Sofia has an extensive <a href="/wiki/Toplofikatsiya_Sofia" title="Toplofikatsiya Sofia">district heating system</a> based around four <a href="/wiki/Cogeneration" title="Cogeneration">combined heat and power</a> (CHP) plants and <a href="/wiki/Heat-only_boiler_station" title="Heat-only boiler station">boiler stations</a>. Virtually the entire city (900,000 households and 5,900 companies) is centrally heated, using residual heat from <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">electricity generation</a> (3,000 <a href="/wiki/Watt" title="Watt">MW</a>) and gas- and oil-fired heating furnaces; total <a href="/wiki/Thermal_mass" title="Thermal mass">heat capacity</a> is 4,640 MW. The heat distribution piping network is 900&#160;km (559&#160;mi) long and comprises 14,000 substations and 10,000 heated buildings.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_University_9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Sofia_University_9.jpg/220px-Sofia_University_9.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Sofia_University_9.jpg/330px-Sofia_University_9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Sofia_University_9.jpg/440px-Sofia_University_9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_University_9.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
One of the lecturing halls in the Rectorate of <a href="/wiki/Sofia_University" title="Sofia University">Sofia University</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sofia concentrates a significant portion of the national <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a> capacity, including 109,000 university and college students<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> and 22 of Bulgaria's 51 higher education establishments.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> These include four of the five highest-ranking national universities ‚Äì <a href="/wiki/Sofia_University" title="Sofia University">Sofia University</a> (SU), <a href="/wiki/University_of_Architecture,_Civil_Engineering_and_Geodesy" title="University of Architecture, Civil Engineering and Geodesy">University of Architecture, Civil Engineering and Geodesy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Technical_University_of_Sofia" class="mw-redirect" title="Technical University of Sofia">Technical University of Sofia</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_National_and_World_Economy" title="University of National and World Economy">University of National and World Economy</a> and the University of Mining and Geology.<sup id="cite_ref-Webometrics_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Webometrics-157">[157]</a></sup> Sofia University was founded in 1888.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> More than 20,000 students<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> study in its 16 faculties.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> A number of research and cultural departments operate within SU, including its own publishing house, <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical gardens</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> a space research centre, a <a href="/wiki/Quantum_electronics" class="mw-redirect" title="Quantum electronics">quantum electronics</a> department,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Confucius_Institute" title="Confucius Institute">Confucius Institute</a><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rakovski_Defence_and_Staff_College" title="Rakovski Defence and Staff College">Rakovski Defence and Staff College</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Arts" title="National Academy of Arts">National Academy of Arts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Medical_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Sofia Medical University">Sofia Medical University</a> are other major higher education establishments in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Webometrics_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Webometrics-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are 5 primary, 77 middle and 187 secondary schools, of all 77 are private. Education institutions include 13 specialized for children with disabilities, 8 art schools, 22 professional colleges. 35 professional high schools, 25 profiled high schools and 4 sport schools.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> The "elite" secondary language schools provide education in a selected foreign language. These include the First English Language School, Sofia High School of Mathematics, 91st German Language School, 164th Spanish Language School, and 9th French Language School. Some of them provide a language certificate upon graduation, while the 9th French Language School has exchange programs with a number of <i>lyc√©es</i> in France and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, such as the Parisian <a href="/wiki/Coll%C3%A8ge-lyc%C3%A9e_Jacques-Decour" title="Coll√®ge-lyc√©e Jacques-Decour">Coll√®ge-lyc√©e Jacques-Decour</a>. The <a href="/wiki/American_College_of_Sofia" title="American College of Sofia">American College of Sofia</a>, a private secondary school which developed from a school founded by American missionaries in 1860, is among the oldest American educational institutions outside of the US.<sup id="cite_ref-ACS_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACS-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other institutions of national significance, such as the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Bulgarian Academy of Sciences">Bulgarian Academy of Sciences</a> (BAS) and the <a href="/wiki/SS._Cyril_and_Methodius_National_Library" title="SS. Cyril and Methodius National Library">SS. Cyril and Methodius National Library</a> are located in Sofia. BAS is the centrepiece of scientific research in Bulgaria, employing more than 4,500 scientists in various institutes, including the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Space_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian Space Agency">Bulgarian Space Agency</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooperation_agreements">Cooperation agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cooperation agreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addition Sofia has cooperation agreements with:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary"><img alt="Hungary" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/35px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/46px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, Hungary<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, France<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal"><img alt="Portugal" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/23px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/35px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/45px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, Portugal<sup id="cite_ref-Lisbon_twinnings_2_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lisbon_twinnings_2-174">[174]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honour">Honour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Honour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Serdica_Peak" title="Serdica Peak">Serdica Peak</a> on <a href="/wiki/Livingston_Island" title="Livingston Island">Livingston Island</a> in the <a href="/wiki/South_Shetland_Islands" title="South Shetland Islands">South Shetland Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> is named after Serdica.</p>
